text:
They ARE the best meatballs, even though I use all beef most of the time. I don't fry, b/c I am too impatient, and the meatballs break up more that way. I scoop them out with a spoon, roll them in my hands, and bake on a cake rack in the oven over a foil-lined cookie sheet. This way, they brown nicely, excess fat is drained off, and they can go right into sauce, or, in our family, meatball hoagies, along with sauteed onions and peppers. They also freeze very well when baked this way. When I take these to parties, I always get requests for the recipe.

text:
This is soooo close to my Nonna's authentic Italian recipe! I am telling you, these meatballs ROCK! Uh oh, the word is out!!! How funny! 3 meats, the breadcrumbs, plus 1 egg. You can also use fresh chopped spinach instead of parsley (or 1 pkg frozen, thawed and all water squeezed out) and pecorino romano cheese instead of parmesan. I make sure I have these on hand almost all the time, I use one lb of EACH meat, and it makes 30-40. Instead of frying, I par bake mine on a cookie sheet at 325 for about 10 minutes, then set the tray (if room allows) into the freezer for an hour or so. Pop them off the tray, into a couple of large freezer bags. Meatballs on demand!! Drop them into a sauce or steam in a glass casserole dish for about 5 minutes, they will be medium-well on the inside. Absolute crowd pleaser if you are making a big Italian dinner!!

text:
There is nothing I hate more than to get a mediocre or worse review from people who do not follow the recipe as written, and then judge YOU on it. I followed this to a "T" even though my experience as a chef was telling me not to. Too much cheese. Not enough garlic. And "salt and pepper to taste" is a personal pet peeve. If you are going to post a recipe, include all the measurements, or be prepared to take your lumps. This recipe is good enough to avoid disaster, but DO NOT FRY. They stick to the pan and melt away when you add them to the gravy(tomato sauce). Instead, bake them for about 35 minutes at 350. Then, put them in the gravy for the last hour or two. Replace half the cheese with more breadcrumbs. Less mess, healthier and easier.

text:
Honestly, I was skeptical using water in a meatball recipe, but it was really great!  I scaled to 4 servings, used only beef, 85%, 1/2 cup italian style breadcrumbs and Kraft parmesan cheese, as my young children do not yet appreciate the stronger flavor of "real" cheese, and they both said they were the best meatballs ever.  Also, I did not fry them, to cut down on fat and clean-up, and they kept their shape just fine.  I just put them in the gravy and cooked them on simmer for 30 minutes.  The sauce was a simple marinara, just sautee 2 cloves of garlic, add 3 cans of crushed tomatoes, 1 can paste, 3/4 c. water and simmer.  Add 1T oregano, 1t. basil, 1t. onion powder, salt and pepper and voila!  Geanine and I teamed up to make an awesome dinner!  Thanks Geanine!

text:
This IS the best Italian Meatball recipe ever.  My ex-mother-in-law gave me this recipe more than 25 years ago.  We use italian style breadcrumbs and much less liquid (about 1/4 cup milk). What makes it so good is the ratio of meats.  You can adjust the flavorings to suit your family's taste.  Once browned, the meatballs can finish cooking in the frypan or by baking, or even add them to the sauce.  I would recommend this basic recipe to anyone.  Excellent addition to Allrecipes.com.

text:
These definitely are some of "The Best Meatballs"! Using three types of meat really makes a difference and a good rule of thumb to ensure moistness is one egg for every one pound of meat. These were delicious - so good you almost could eat them by themselves, but even better when accompanied by an equally good spaghetti sauce. I used a compination of Parmesan and Romano cheeses. I put the Italian bread into my mini food processor and gave it a whirl to produce bread crumbs. Instead of water I used milk and only enough for the meatballs to hold their shape. You don't want these to be mushy or falling apart. I didn't use the olive oil to fry them in a pan but instead I put these into a baking dish and baked at 350 for 20-25 minutes. These were very moist and full of flavor -excellent recipe!

text:
I have my own "best meatballs" but every now and then I like to try something different. What I particularly liked about this recipe was the combination of three meats, the addition of Romano cheese (Parmesan would work equally as well), and the fact that it's not loaded up with commercial "Italian Seasoning."  But I did back off on the cheese to 1/2 cup and added twice as much garlic - I think the amount of cheese called for is far too much.  I also used milk rather than water, just enough for the bread to absorb, then squeezed it dry.  I didn't want the mess of frying, so I took the easy way out and baked them on a large cookie sheet at 400 degrees for about 20-25 minutes.  At that point I tossed them in the Crock-pot with some of my homemade tomato sauce and let it all marry for several hours.  This made a LOT of meatballs for Hubs and me, and was just what I had in mind for easy meals for the next couple of nights while we take care of last minute packing and preparations for our return to Italy! There was even enough to give a good amount to Mom! While I'll always be partial to "my own" way of making meatballs (actually Grandma's and Mom's meatballs I grew up on), this was a pretty darned good meatball (backing off on the cheese), with just a few simple ingredients.

text:
I only gave this four stars because I feel the olive oil and the water are so unnecessary. If you are using ground pork in your meatballs, trust me, there will be plenty of grease to keep them moist and delicious. No need whatsoever to add additional oils. And the water? That I truly don't understand at all. I make these without either the oil or water and they are super moist and extremely delicious!! Without those two unnecessary ingredients, and the addition of basil this easily goes to five stars and above!! Oh, I also do not fry my meatballs. I use a cookie scoop to make them a uniform size and drop them onto a cookie sheet lined with no stick foil (for super easy cleanup and easy removal from thee pan). I bake them for 40 minutes at 350 degrees F. Then I add some to my sauce and freeze the rest for another day, another meal. These are GREAT for meatball sandwiches!!

text:
This meatball recipe is great! I just made them this evening for dinner and they came out great...I changed a couple of things, but it still came out great! I used ground beef only.  I substituted italian style breadcrumbs for the bread as Michelle suggested in her review, and I added some italian seasoning as well as parsley and basil to the meat mixture, I found no need for the water and the oil, so I omitted the water and the oil.  I find that baking meatballs is so much better and healthier than frying, and they seem to keep their shape better also.  The trick to this is, not to over bake them because they can dry out quickly if you don't keep an eye on them so I just use my timer on the oven and it works great, but don't cook them for more than 30 mins in the over.  I put a very light coat of oil on a glass pan, you can also use cooking spray as well. I cooked the meatballs on 350 for 20 minutes while I was preparing the sauce and then added a few extra minutes to complete the sauce.  As soon as, I got the sauce started I put the meatballs in right away and simmered them with the sauce for about an hour, every thing came out great!  Maybe it depends on the size of the meatballs also, but I made mine the size of golf balls, if they cook for only 30 mins they're more than likely not going to be cooked all the way through, but they will finish cooking with the sauce simmering for about an hour, plus some of the fat from the meat will give the sauce lots of flavor!

text:
This was my first attempt at meatballs and they came out great! I only had about 1 1/2 lb of 80/20 ground beef, so I tweaked the recipe accordingly. I still used 2 cloves of garlic, 2 eggs, regular dried parsley, and equal parts salt and pepper. I kind of tossed in around 1/2-3/4 cup grated cheese, around 1 cup of Italian bread crumbs, and about 1/2 cup olive oil. I didn't add any water to the mix since it was perfect as is and I fried the meatballs in olive oil until browned. I then added them to my sauce and let them simmer for about an hour. They were some of the best meatballs I've ever had! This is definitely a great base meatball recipe!

text:
I love these meatballs - they are so tasty.  I use all three meats, and asiago cheese instead of Romano (what I had in the house).  I also microplane an onion and add it to the mix, cutting back the water by about a 1/2 cut (since the microplaned onion is pretty watery.  Adds a nice flavor.  I also use dried parsley flakes as I hate buying a huge bunch for 1 1/2 tablespoons.  I use a large cookie scoop to make my meatballs a nice even size.  Like others, I bake my meatballs in the oven on cookie sheets at 375 for about 25 mins and at 350 for another 15 minutes. I freeze half of the meatballs and keep the other half available in the frig.  Try 'em, you'll like 'em!

text:
This is the typical Italian meatball recipe - best to use Italian bread crumbs (I freeze left-over bread and take out as much as I need).  I soak it in water - milk  is also OK - squeeze the liquid out and add the crumbs to the meat with the other ingredients - frying was what was always used, but most of us want to eat more healthfully and bake  them.  I add them to tomato sauce and let it simmer for a long time - 1-2 hours usually - the meatballs really get the flavor of the sauce.  Dropping raw meatballs in sauce does not appeal to me (my preference) - I feel the fat in the meatballs adds up in the sauce - frying or baking does release some of the fat.  My opinion only.
But am happy to see that so many people are going back to so many original recipes.

text:
To reduce the fat significantly, I bake the meatballs at 400F until a meat thermometer comes out to 145-150F (about 30 minutes, depending on your oven).  This makes less mess, less fat, and they taste yummy.  I then put the cooked meatballs into the marinara sauce and simmer in a slow cooker.  Also, instead of water in the meatballs, try milk instead.  Last, I always use ground beef, no pork nor veal.  They still come out delicious and have a bit less fat.

text:
Sorry to do this but I did change the recipe a bit.  I used 1# of gr. beef and 1/2# of mild Italian sausage.  Used an Italian herb mix, parsley, garlic and dried red onion.  To that I added 1/2 c. bread crumbs (made from several-day old sturdy white bread) which I mixed with 1/4 c. of milk.  Let the bread crumb/milk mixture sit long enough to let the crumbs absorb the milk before adding to the meat mixture.  Added 1/2 c. grated parmesan and 2 eggs, a teaspoon each of salt and pepper.  Mixed everything up well and used my cookie scoop to make perfect size meatballs.  Baked in the oven (350 degrees) for 30 minutes.  This made 23 meatballs (a little smaller than golf ball size).  Perfect!  Thank you, Geanine, for submitting this recipe, without it I wouldn't have had good meatballs.

Have made these time and time again as stated and altering slightly with what I have on hand. text:
THIS is coming from an Italian who has made her meatballs like this recipe for years just like my mom made.  Only difference is I soak my Italian bread in water and squeeze out the liquid and crumble it into the meat and use milk instead of water for more moisture.  So glad the video emphasized using FRESH ITALIAN PARSLEY and not the curly stuff.  Also the fresh garlic and the good grated cheese are what makes these over the top.  
PLEASE, PLEASE NEVER COOK THE MEATBALLS IN THE SAUCE.  You won't get that crispy outside, just boiled meat. Some people roll their meatballs in bread crumb before frying. You could put them in the oven, but I like frying best.

text:
I spent 17 summers in Italy and have had amazing meatballs and never could find a recipe that I loved until now! I use Italian seasoned breadcrumbs & bake the meatballs first. I have tried it with the 3 meat combinations and I've also done it with just beef. The 3 meat combo is the best, but don't hesitate to try this with just beef if that's all you have. I do bake mine for 17 minutes at 400 degrees on a cookie sheet.  I used to bake at 350, but the inside juice will all come out of the meatball. you want to cook at higher temp so it tramps in the ingredients/flavor! As far as the amount of water, I use the amount directed. You know it's the right consistency if, after the ingredients are all fully mixed, it doesn't stick to the bowl....the full meat mixture adheres together, if meat sticks to your fingers in clumps, it's too moist. (I did use too much water once and the meatballs fell apart). A mistake I can see many making is not using enough sea salt. You need a considerable amount.  I just used 6 lbs of ground meat and used a handful of salt. If you follow the recipe given you would probably need 2 heaping tablespoons of sea salt. You cannot just sprinke some salt and think that's enough. you need a decent amount. Finally, what really will give your meatballs 5 stars is the sauce you put them in!

I've been making meatballs for 50 years and have realized that just putting them in the sauce for 20 minutes (no more than 20 minutes) allows for the tenderist, moistest, most delicious meatballs ever.

text:
I made these this past weekend. The mixture is the same as my Italian Nana's. It only needs 1/2 cup of water, and you need to let the mixture rest for about 30 min. before you make the balls.  Heat olive oil to med. high, gently roll them,under cook, and drain, before you add then to your "gravy" sauce. I usually build my sauce in the same pot as I saute the meatballs in so I can take up all the tasty little bits.

FANTASTIC!!!  I (and family) loved this recipe...only change was that i did not have dry stale bread to crumble so I used 2 cups Italian seasoned bread crumbs.  I also used a couple more cloves of garlic since we like garlic.. I fried in only a couple teaspoons of olive oil, that's all you really need, a cup seems much.  Olive oil is actually good for you so I did not mind.  I also added a couple tablespoons of worcheshire to half the mix to see if they would taste different...it added a tiny bit more flavor, but w/o is just as good.  I also baked at 350 for 20 more minutes just to make sure they cooked all the way.  This is my new meatball recipe for life!  p.s. MAKE SURE TO USE ROMANO CHEESE like recipe calls for AND NOT PARMESAN, tastes better.

text:
This is a great basic meatball recipe! I modified the recipe for what I had on hand and from reading other reviews. I used 1lb ground Italian pork sausage (such as Jimmy Deans) and 1 pound of ground turkey because it is what I had on hand. I also substituted 1 cup of dried Italian bread crumbs in place of the stale bread and used grated parmesan cheese instead of fresh romano. I also used 1/2 cup milk instead of water. I baked these meatballs in the oven for 30 minutes at 350Â° and then added them to my sauce. My Husband and I both raved about the meatballs and we over ate because they were so good. We even fought about who got the take the left overs the next day for lunch. Truly a great starter recipe and I love that cheaper/easier substitutions can be made and they are still great.

text:
Thank you, Geanine!  I had to make some adjustments and according to my family, they're still 5-star quality: 1) doubled the recipe - as long as your taking the time to fry these, make it worth your while, 2) no veal at my grocery store, so replaced with ground chuck (80/20%) - thus, it's 3 pounds ground chuck and 1 pound ground pork; 3) cost of fresh grated Romano was out of my budget, so one, 8 oz. plastic shaker of a  50/50% Romano/Parmesan blend; 4) no stale Italian bread on hand, so 1 1/4 cup of Italian bread crumbs for a double recipe.
While I agree with Geanine that freshly grated cheese and bread crumbs may be more flavorful, the prepared cheese and bread crumbs are much more time-efficient and cost-effective.

text:
Very good recipe! Mixing two or three kinds of meat
is a very good idea. Also water in the mixture is a must for really soft meatballs. Rolling the balls in flour before frying helps to keep them in perfect shape. If you prefer not to fry it is not necessary. Cooking them directly in a sauce or baking them also is very good, this way you avoid loads of calories and much healthier. Another good practice is to use old bread, preferably whole wheat, instead of dry bread crumbs, soaked in water. Using different spices one prefers also is good idea. These meatballs are really great for parties!

I just found this recipe on here and compared it to my own that I have used for many years.  I NEVER add water to my recipe. The eggs in the mix keep the meatballs moist! Also I use seasoned breadcrumbs & add more italian seasoning to the mix as well as onion powder. Add pepperoni & braised brasciole for a real italian sauce.

I have made this recipe  three times now.  This has now became my standard recipe.  These are the best I have every made and I always get compliments!
I will say for those of you that have not used the beef AND pork AND veal, you are not making the same meatballs so reviewing this recipe is really useless.  The three meats are really a classic. With well over 700 reviews is seems a bit redundant to add another but these were so good I just have to. 
Like others I baked them in the oven. Started off at 350 but then bumped it up closer to 400. Next time I'll do it all at 375. Took 20 min for the larger balls and about 10 to 12 for the smaller. I placed the larger balls on a cookie rack over a sheet and the smaller ones on parchment lined rimmed sheets. By far the best way is the parchment paper. Super easy clean-up.
I have been looking for a long time for the perfect meatball recipe and this is it - I am so happy to finally have this wonderful recipe. Many many huge thanks to Geanine for submitting and thanks also to other reviewers for all their input and suggestions.

Great recipe and the meatballs were delicious.  The fresh cheese and crumbled, stale Italian bread instead of canned breadcrumbs really does make a difference.  I had to make a few changes though as I couldn't find ground veal in any stores in my area, so I just used a half and half mixture of ground beef and pork. I like this recipe.  I really did.  We cut this recipe in half (only because it is just my husband and I), so please note these changes are made for FOUR servings instead of eight.  I made a few changes.  We made it with all ground beef.  Instead of stale bread, we used one cup of italian bread crumbs.  We used 1/4 cup eggbeaters instead of the egg.  As for the water, out of the "1/2 cup at a time" I only put about 2 TB of water altogether.  It held up really, really well. I pan fried my meatballs with just about 2 TB of olive oil. I used the pasta sauce from Wolfgang puck's website and used spaghetti rigati and it was FABULOUS (according to my husband).  Enjoy everyone!!!

country:
None
text:
This is very close to my recipe also. I use about 2 lbs of good ground beef and just under 1 lb. of Johnsonville mild Italian sausage. I add 1 Tbsp of Oregano, 1 Tbsp of Parsley and 1 Tbsp of Sweet Basil. I also cut off about 2/3 of a 2 foot French Bread Loaf and run it thru the food processor to make very coarse fresh bread crumbs.  Plus a good amount of salt and pepper, garlic, and grated Parmesan cheese and 1 or 2 eggs. Thoroughly mix all ingredients and add the warm water in 3 doses while mixing by hand. I usually get about 1 1/2 cups in. Final mixture should be very soft. The warm water helps to make it sticky so when you're rolling the meatballs around in your hands they stay together very well. Bake or Fry in oil until brown, drain, add to your favorite sauce and cook for another 30 minutes.

text:
This recipe is a great place to start for basic ingredients that will produce a moist meatball that holds its shape. BUT, they're a bit bland for my taste. 

I use this recipe as my "beginning" and add oregano, basil, and a bit of chili powder. I just "eyeball" it and each time has come out just fine. I add salt and pepper and then taste one after its done cooking. If they need more, I sprinkle a bit additional at that point.

I've been cooking these in the oven as some other reviewers suggested and then place them in the sauce to finish cooking. It imparts a nice flavor to the sauce without the addition of the grease from the meat.

ALSO - one of the most critical components of this meatball is the fresh parsley. The parsley adds a wonderfully fresh flavor. Don't substitute with dried, it won't be the same.

text:
I made these again last night (doubling the recipe to have more on hand) but did tweak it some and found them fantastic!  First I used 2lb's lean ground beef, 1lb. lean ground turkey and 1 lb. ground pork.  I also used only 1 & 1/2 cup liquid (red wine in lieu of water) instead of doubling it and found it to be just enough for the doubled recipe.  I added a few more garlic cloves and 2 med. sized minced onion and used 1 C grated asiogo and 1C Kraft parmesan & about 1 T of red pepper flakes.  I found baking them at 325 for 20 min to be an easy way to keep them lower in fat (turning about every 5 min or so) and they came out very nice & moist and MUCH lower in fat than frying.  My husband and I  LOVED them!  I have tons more on hand that I froze and will be enjoying these again & again!

Wow, these were great and easy.  I made two batches for a Christmas Party.  I actually baked them on a rack over a cookie sheet. text:
Great recipe!  I've made these probably about 5 or 6 times over the past few months.  I took the advice of many reviewers and now have the perfect recipe for my family's liking:  sautee 1/2 finely chopped onion with the garlic cloves and let cool before adding to meat ball mixture; sometimes I use 1.5 lbs ground beef w/ 1/2 lb pork (the veal can give the meatballs a gamey flavor); sometimes I add a little fresh basil; and I bake for about 15 minutes in the oven.  I pop them in the freezer for a great insta-meal for my 14 month old twins, or I heat up in sauce for the adults.  Delish!

text:
These meatballs are delicious but I have to be honest...I had to tweak the recipe because I didn't have all the ingredients... I replaced the Romano Cheese with some Parmesan (store bought) and the Italian bread with Wonderbread Light Wheat bread. And the meat I used was a pre-mix of Beef/Veal/Pork for meatballs and meatloaf... "Catelli Italian Bistro Meatball/Meatloaf mix)...it was about 1.3 lbs of meat... and saved me the trouble ;)  I also used a little less water. Possibly about 3/4 of a cup to 1 cup... I put all the ingredients except the meat and eggs in my chopper so that the cheese parsley and garlic would mix well... I beat 2 eggs and added the eggs and cheese/garlic/parsley to the meat (which was lightly seasoned adobo) and mixed everything by hand.  I took the chopper and used 2 1/2 almost 3 slices of wonder wheat bread and made my own bread crumbs.  I threw that in and kept mixing everything added some salt and pepper... I took a cup of water and added slowly like the directions said but never finished the whole cup.  I also took about 1/2 cup of olive oil and threw that in on top at the end so that it would get sticky and keep the balls together.  I baked at 400 degrees for 22 minutes (or so)... and came out with 24 meatballs about golf size... threw some in my spahetti sauce and my 6 year old ate 4 alone (she doesn't like "red" spaghetti sauce)... Simply delicious... I would say 4.5 stars cause you don't really need that much water!! Still great anyway!!!

The only suggestion I can make to this is add 2 dashes Worchester and 1 cup of bread crumbs instead of 2.  Add Water and milk to the consistency you like, a tad mushy but still able to hold shape.  If you use to much bread crumbs it masks the flavor of the meat.  I have tried this recipe to a "T" and those are the only tweaks I would make.

text:
These are great, I've made them twice now.  Of course, I adjusted it a bit to my tastes but I still think the original recipe deserves 5 stars.  But that aside, here are my changes:  I only use beef (we don't eat pork), I cut the recipe in 1/2, I doubled the garlic, I used the Parmesan Blend cheese from Walmart and I didn't measure it so I'm sure I used too much, and I used fresh bread crumbs and left out the water since the bread wasn't dry.  I also don't bother adding any oil to fry them, just a quick spray of Pam to keep them from sticking.  Oh and I also added a couple of teaspoons of italian seasoning.  Man when you write it all down it doesn't sound like I followed the recipe at all LOL.  But they are delicous!  My husband loved them too and he is P I C K Y.

country:

text:
I would definitely make this again and it takes great with or without red sauce.  The changes I made were only because of what I had on hand - I did not have fresh bread crumbs, unfortunately, so used Progresso Italian breadcrumbs but only 1 cup.  Used 1/4 cup milk instead of water because I thought it might add a bit more depth of flavor,  used 1 pound of veal instead of 1/2 and then baked instead of fried since I don't need any more oils even if they are "good" oils. 
 On the baking sheets - I used two - I put several tablespoons of extra virgin olive oil on the sheets and nothing on the other sheet.  The sheet with the olive oil was on the bottom of the oven and browned considerably more than the one at the top of the oven but they both tasted exactly the same.   I baked for 30 minutes at 400F because I had to go somewhere and didn't want to leave the oven on and they were perfectly cooked but not pink - more medium. If you want them to be medium rare I suggest you taste them after 20 minutes or cook for 30 at 350 instead of 400F.  Especially if you will be cooking them in tomato sauce after the oven.

text:
I reworked the recipe to yield more to lower fat due to health issues. 

Approx. 1 pound of the leanest ground beef
Approx. 1/4 cup of Romano Cheese
2 eggs
Approx. 1 cup Italian bread crumbs
2 cloves of garlic cut up finely
Approx. 1/2 cup of onions cut in small, fine pieces

Mix together in large bowl. Roll into balls and put on a cookie sheet with tin foil on bottom.  Bake in oven at 350Â° for 35 minutes or depending on how big you bake your meatballs. Add to sauce.

These were delicious! I made them for the first time just now and made the following adjustments to recipe:

My husband raved over these and he isn't even a fan of meatballs. They were really good and I will definitely be making these again! They were mild flavored and no particular flavor dominated making them perfect to showcase the delicious sauce I put them in. I cut this in half and only used ground beef. I only had white sandwich bread(2 slices), canned shredded Parmesan and Romano, and regular dried parsley. I added 1/2 c. milk instead of the water. I did have to be really careful turning these as they had a tendency to try and fall apart, but once the outsides were browned they held together just fine as long as I was careful with them. I let these simmer in the sauce for about 15 minutes while I was preparing the pasta and salad. My husband doesn't usually rave about a meal but this one he did. I agree these were tasty and were perfect with the homemade spaghetti sauce. I used a cookie scoop to make the meatballs and then only made 14 or so for tonight and froze the rest for later. This gave me 31 meatballs just from the lb. of meat. Thanks for fantastic recipe Geanine! We love this.

text:
These meatballs are delicious! I was looking for a meatball recipe that makes soft meatballs and this is it. I used only beef, added finely minced onions (as is my personal preference), and used milk instead of water (as some other reviewers suggested). I made ping pong sized balls and baked them at 350 degrees F for about 45 minutes, instead of frying. Then I added them to the sauce and served with pasta. I froze leftovers, popped them off the pan, and stored them in a bag in the freezer for another meal. For an easy meal, I just re-heated the frozen meatballs in sauce. We got two meals out of this recipe for our family of three with hearty appetites. We'll definitely make this often.

text:
I have been making my meatballs like this for several years and they truly are the best.  I did make a few adjustments which I think made these even better....I mix the meat, eggs, cheese and fresh parsley first.  I use fresh bread and make my own breadcrumbs using my mini food processor. Don't be afraid to go heavy on the fresh bread crumbs as it is what makes these so soft and tender!  I then use warm chicken broth( no sodium ) in place of the water as I beleive it adds more flavor!  I add about 1/4 cup at a time until the meat is very moist.  I  prefer to bake the meatballs in the oven at 350 for about 20 minutes. I usually make a double batch and freeze some .  Add meatballs to the sauce and simmer away.  Simply the best!!!

text:
I altered the ingredients and cooking method a tiny bit, so I'd give the version I made a 4.5, but I'm confident that if this were followed exactly they'd be a 5. These turned out yummy. 

My changes: I only used 1 pound of 80/20 ground beef so I halved the rest of the recipe (it yielded about 23 meatballs) and replaced the Romano with some shredded Parmesan I had in the fridge.  I also nixed the oil since I baked them in the oven. I baked them on a foil-lined cookie sheet at 325 degrees for about 25 minutes, then I put the oven on broil and let them cook for a minute or so. They were very juicy but I could've left them on broil a little longer to get them crispier. 

This was served over whole wheat penne with an out-of-the-jar version of tomato-pesto sauce... So yummy and relatively quick! I will be eating some leftover meatballs in a sandwich for lunch.

I made this exactly as written as I really don't think it's fair to make too many changes to a recipe and then review it.  Too much cheese, not enough garlic, not enough bread crumbs.  My meatballs were woefully under-seasoned.  I ate one on it's own first - bland.  I ate a 2nd one that I added salt and pepper to and it was much better.  I hate recipes that say "salt and pepper to taste".  That's fine if I'm making a sauce and I can taste as I go (although a starting point would be good i.e. 1/4 tsp. salt and increase to taste).  This is raw meat that you can't taste until it's fully cooked and too late.  I was worried that the Romano cheese would make them too salty and wish I'd seasoned more heavily.  I would also have used twice the garlic.  I MAY try these again but kind of doubt it.

text:
I make this recipe every time I make meatballs, but I change a couple of things (I hate when reviewers do this, too, but it helps when you don't have everything in the kitchen):

I use only ground beef, I never have the parsley so I leave it out, canola oil instead of olive, I will sub in a little milk or half and half for some of the water, and Trader Joes Romano/Parmesan mixture (the one off of the shelf) instead of just fresh Romano.  I have used both regular Italian bread crumbs and gluten-free bread crumbs, and they both come out delicious. I make the gluten-free ones when my gluten-free people come over - they love it with the Udi's gluten-free bread and mozzarella cheese.  Yummy gluten-free meatball parm!

I brown them in the oil and then the key is using Rao's Marinara pasta sauce to let it simmer for an hour or so (the next day it's even better.)  The sauce is on the expensive side, but it is truly the best sauce for meatballs.

I did tweak it a bit, but the basic ingredients were an awesome delight.  Instead of stale bread crumbs I used asiago cheese bread and pulsed it in my food processor.  Instead of salt, I added 1.5 tsp. beef base past and 1 tsp pork base to the 1.5 cups of water.  I didn't have Romano cheese so substituted fresh parmesan.  I think the asiago bread made up for the difference. I also used a small ice cream scooper and never had to touch the mixture.  The final results were awesome!!

text:
I make my meatballs using equal parts ground beef and ground turkey. I also bake them. Just line your pan with parchment paper and they will come out perfectly round and they just roll off the paper. I also wear nitrile gloves when mixing the meats, spices, egg and breadcrumbs and also when shaping them. Keeps your hands clean and wear and tear of the skin. Adding an egg to the meat mixture helps to hold the meat together.

I got a little carried away. I misread the original recipe, and added about a cup of parsley, plus I added a sauted onion. Instead of Italian bread I used Planko instead, had it on hand. also added some mozarelle I needed to use up.AND, ( I told you I got carried away), instead of water, I used some red wine. Now I know there is debate about whether to cook your meatballs in the sauce, or pre-brown (which I have always done in past), so I did 50-50. Used a tomato-basil sauce, and added some fresh mushrooms. This was a FEAST! The meatballs were the star!!! I used all beef, 93% lean, but I figured the extra cheese made it less so. All in all, the original recipe is a great base recipe. By the way, added some red win to the chef too! :).

text:
I used the ingredients exactly as outlined and these meatballs were just alright. Quite heavy on the parmesan for me... I par-baked them as another user suggested and finished cooking them in a homemade marinara sauce - Big Mistake! Definitely cook these meatballs completely before adding to any kind of sauce. Otherwise they render a ton of grease and leach a lot of parmesan into the sauce, clouding it up.  I'm not positive but I think frying/baking them completely (as the recipe says) would help mitigate the leaching.  Definitely couldn't hurt to have less cheese in there to begin with... The meat should be the star here!

I recently had dinner at a place in Toronto known as "the nose" and one of their signature dishes is an appetizer of one giant meatball swimming in sauce with shavings of asiago. We are trying to watch our weight but got really sick of raw veggie diet.  We decided to make something tasty but yet wouldn't jeopardize what we've lost.  This was just the recipe we wanted... water and cheese in meatballs... who knew? (at least I didn't). After looking at the nutritional value, we decided to make a few changes... half the cheese and bread crumbs. In addition, we added worchestire sauce, sicilian bread dipping salt, and mustard for flavor... instead of frying, we pan fried which eliminated a lot of the fat from the meat... and of course, portion control, smaller balls. End result... YUMMY!  The smell was amazing the whole process...

text:
I hate to rate a recipe I've made changes to but this deserves 5 stars  before my changes.   
I won't go into which types of meat to use, ground veal in not commonly available in my area, we tend to let the cattle get a bit bigger before we knock 'em in the head. 
I use lean meats and sometimes a mixture of Romano and Parmesan cheese,  fresh grated.  
The one thing I do that I think really sets this off is I use Chianti wine  instead of water.   Or sometimes a Shiraz.  
I bake mine on  a rack so they drain in a hot oven to an internal temp of 155.   With a hot oven (375) it does a nice crust on the exterior.  You just have to pull them quick.  I roll mine by hand about the size of a golf ball or even a bit bigger. This keeps the cheese from all melting out.

This is one we batch cook in a large about, 5 times what the recipe calls for.   We freeze them.  These are great when we go camping.

text:
One situation I began with is the ground pork and ground veal are only sold in my area frozen in 1 lb packs.  So therefore, I used 1 lb each of ground veal and ground pork and 2 lbs of ground beef.  I also increased the eggs.  Since I wasn't sure if the recipe called for large or extra large eggs, I put in 5 extra large eggs and would probably make it 6 extra large eggs when I make this again.  I was able to get 6.5 dozen meatballs from this amount of meat, making them the size of a golf ball.    I also increased the garlic to 6 cloves minced, 4 TB parsley, added 4 TB fresh Basil, Fresh Oregano because I like those seasonings.  I had 4 cups of stale bread and added my milk ( recipe called for water) to the bread to let it soak together. I also increased the milk to 3 cups and did add about another 1/4 cup as the bread really soaked up the milk quickly. I followed one of the other reviewers suggestion and baked the meatballs on parchment paper for 50 minutes at 350, turning them over at 30 minutes. I drained the meatballs on paper towel after coming out of the oven.     I made Chef John's Mushroom Gravy ( found on Allrecipes) and added 2 dozen meatballs for our dinner that night.  I froze the rest to have later.  I plan to make a tomato sauce and or more mushroom gravy or both as we have 4 dozen plus meatballs left.  I would make this recipe again, with these adjustments due to our tastes and style of cooking.

Iâ€™ve made this 3 times now. First and second times exactly as written. This third time I included all ingredients except breadcrumbs and then split it in half. I then soaked breadcrumbs in milk (1/2 recipe) for one part, again exactly as written except milk instead of water. The keto ones were good but texture not as good as the ones with breadcrumbs. My husband liked them better when I fried them. They browned up more. Although it was so much easier and way less mess to cleanup baking them. I put them on a cookie rack while baking. Next time Iâ€™m going to try to baking them right on the tin foil and see if that is more browned/fried tasting for my husband.  This is such a good recipe! Thanks for sharing.

text:
I'm sure veal would have been great but here is what I used and they turned out great!  Ground beef, hot Italian sausage and ground turkey (I had all this already).  I didn't have bread so I used breadcrumbs but roughly half the amount to account for commercial bread crumbs (tiny) versus crumbled bread.  I did fry them in olive oil, just watch your heat originally, it has a lower heat point then other oils.  Once I got that down everything went smoothly!  I also used stacking cookie racks, lined them with paper towels and let them drain/rest there.  

I reserved some of the last of the mixture (I doubled it) to add some extra savory bits to some lasagna for Christmas! Yum!

text:
I'm gonna do all ya'll a favor.... Follow the recipe but brown the meatballs in olive oil in a cast iron skillet, remove from pan and turn the heat down. Add a small amount of butter and chopped garlic to the pan, cook for about a minute, re-add the meatballs, and place in oven at 350 until cooked all the way through. Mine didn't fall apart like other reviewers said. Definitely use real block grated cheese. I did place a few meatballs in simmering homemade marinara to finish cooking to test and much preferred the garlicy oven finished ones.

text:
Couldn't find my go-to meatball recipe recently but found this one and it looks really similar.  I was making really large meatballs to be cooked on the smoker, so I doubled the recipe from the get-go.  No intentional changes made ... I do think I only ended up using half the amount of breadcrumbs (2 cups for a double batch) -- we had company over while I was putting these together and I was distracted and didn't realize until afterwards that I think I'd forgotten to double the breadcrumbs amount.  However, I also noticed as I was working the mixture that I didn't need to add the water at all.  I think next time I make these I'll hold back half of the breadcrumbs and see how they come together and then add in the other half if or as needed along with any water.

Delicious! The family loved them.  I ended up with 54 meatballs which was enough for dinner and then one package to go in the freezer for a future meal.

text:
I don't use veal, I use 1 pound 93 percent hamburg 1 1/2 pounds and 1/2 pound lean ground pork.  Rather than add water to the meatballs, I use the sauce that I make prior to making the meatballs.  I don't bake or fry the meatballs, I put them in the already bubbling sauce.  I cook the meatballs in the bubbling sauce for about 15 minutes, reduce the heat and simmer everything for hours.   As far as the spices in the meatballs, I use a mixture of oregano, basil, thyme, and what ever else I have on hand.  People love my sauce and meatballs.   I improvise just as my grandparents off the boat from Italy.  Never measured, and used what was on hand.

After having found and made this recipe, I now make the best meatballs out of anyone I know.  The combination of the three meats really pushes these meatballs to the head of the line.  I followed the recipe as written, for the most part, but did make a few minor substitutions.  First, I used parmesan cheese, the cheap stuff worked fine,  Then I used closer to three cloves of garlic rather than two.  I subbed store bought panko for the stale bread crumbs the recipe called for.  I only used on 1 cup of water, and I baked them at 350 for around a half hour instead of frying.  They were outstanding and the leftovers froze well.

This was my first time attempting homemade meatballs. I was pleased that they were easy and turned out better than store bought, flavorful and moist, but I don't think I'll make them again. I prefer denser meatballs and even though I barely used 3/4c, the cheese was still very overpowering to me.

This is very close to our family recipe.  I used ground turkey in place of the veal just because that is what I had.  I believe the amount of water called for is more than you need. Great recipe.  The only change I made was to combine the water and eggs and garlic in a bowl then add the seasonings, bread and cheese.  Mix thoroughly till combined and let it sit about 15-30 so dry ingredients can be thoroughly absorbed.  Then I mix in 1/3 of the meat followed by another 1/3 and finally the last 1/3. text:
I've made several types of meatballs over the years, but for me this one has the perfect flavor profile of veal, beef, and pork. They also turn out very tender when baked. That said, I now use this as a base recipe and change a few things as my mood dictates. I bake them, not fry. I don't use water; I use a combination of broth (chix or beef) and/or a little organic 2% milk, probably 1/2 cup or so (organic is thicker and much tastier than regular 2%.) Also the amount of liquid vs breadcrumbs depends on the humidity and type of breadcrumbs you use. One needs to adjust it accordingly. The rule of thumb is that they should be very sticky and slightly sag and lose their shape after rolled into balls. This is so they bake up nice and tender. I throw all the ingedients into my Kitchenaid stand up mixer and it is so easy to combine. I also recently have started replacing some of the other meat with ground turkey (usually the pork or beef) to make it healthier, and it still is great. I also prefer parmesan to romano, which can sometimes make dishes taste salty and sharp.

text:
Used this recipe for my husband's birthday party.  All of his male friends from work came over.  They couldn't get enough!  One even asked me for the recipe telling me he would have his wife make it because the meatballs came out tender and moist.  I did modify it.  Some guests couldn't eat pork for religious reasons.  So I used 100% beef.  I tripled the (fresh) minced garlic and also added a finely diced medium sized onion.  Both garlic and onion were sauteed before adding them to the beef mixture.  I didn't have Romano cheese, but I had leftover mexican 3 cheese blend and italian parmesan.  Since both cheese had herbs and spices, I didn't add the parsley.  Also, I substituted beef broth for the water.  I pan seared these and then placed them in a covered pot with a bit of fat from the saute pan in the oven at 350F for 30 minutes.

text:
Made this a week ago and then again today.  The first time I did it, I made a really stupid mistake, so I'll try and stop you from doing the same thing... This is ALMOST, but not quite a "throw everything in the bowl and mix" kind of recipe.  The olive oil at the end of the recipe is for frying the meatballs.  DUH!  It does NOT go in to the meat mixture.  I can't believe I didn't read the instructions any better than that.  I kept wondering why the mixture was so gooey, and I kept adding more and more bread crumbs!  My excuse is that I was having a really good conversation with my husband while we were cooking, so I was distracted!  LOL!

Bottom line, these will taste good either way, but if you follow the directions, you will enjoy the experience a lot more!

text:
I followed the recipe and made half fried and the other half baked. I personally always fry my meatballs but since they were so flimsy when I fried these, I decided to make them both ways. The meatballs had too much grease on them from the oil in the pan. Ground beef is fatty enough that it shouldn't need it but in this recipe it is absolutely necessary if you expect them to resemble some sort of ball when frying. The water made the meatballs lack any real density and in return, taste. I like my meatballs to have a much heartier taste. I won't be making these again.

I roughly made one third the recipe it's just two of us. Just used ground beef and made it pretty much as written except I had dried parsley. It was quite delicious and very tender and moist. I think the trick is not to over cook the meatballs because they continue to cook in the sauce and the sauce moistens them. I coated a non-stick fry pan with olive oil and just cooked them over medium heat turning them once really, there was no sticking I'm guessing it's because I used nonstick and beef with 15% fat too lean beef will not be good in this recipe. I used Bertoli sauce which is sweet but very good. We inhaled our dinner, thanks.

text:
I wouldn't use the veal or pork as described (1/2 pound sounds like something a butcher's in a big city might have though) so I used the Italian Sausage in place of those two. I tried to make this recipe otherwise as described but since I have celiac disease, I had to use rice cereal crumbs instead of bread crumbs.  But using fresh parmesano and fresh parsley is definitely required!  Once you roll these and start cooking them on medium, let them sit in the pan and cook pretty well before you flip them.  I used tongs.  But the heat under the pan was uneven and some of the meatballs weren't supported and they just flopped into bits when I turned them.  I wonder if more bread crumbs would have helped.  After cooking them pretty well, and browning them on two or more sides, I threw them into simmering homemade spaghetti sauce.  The kids loved them, I loved them and I liked my necessary substitution :).

ETA: tried the 2 cups of GF bread crumbs today (my handmade Udi's crumbs) and there have never been more savory, soft, fluffy meat balls than these, though I merely coated them in oil, then cooked them for 30 mins. at 350 degrees.  I finished them in a loose sauce which I learned from a Sicilian immigrant, which is the perfect way to flavor and spice these delicious, succulent and savory creations.  Bravo!

text:
The recipe as is, is very good. One change as some others have mentioned is to use milk instead of water, and nowhere near as much. Another change is in the method used to cook the meatballs. Bake them in the oven first and then brown them in a frying pan. This will give a much better browning on the outside than baking alone will and they will hold together much better than simply frying them.

text:
I use this recipe as a base and add my own style to it and they consistently make the BEST MEATBALLS EVER!!! Our family is grain free so our meat is more expensive, thus we just use ground beef because it's cheaper. I also replace the bread crumbs with toasted almond meal, saute some finely chopped onions and celery (this helps to add moisture since the texture is different when you use almond vs flour), and I also add fennel and paprika to the mix. I bake them low and slow on a rack over a cake pan so the fat all drips off of them, then kick the temp up for the last few minutes to brown them. SO YUMMY!

text:
Great job Geanine! Loved the basics. I relatively stuck to them. True to form, it got it done. I strongly agree with your recommendation of the mix of meat, fresh herbs, cheese, initial binders. They DO make a difference! 

I did take some culinary license, like some others, in regard to adding a bit of red onion, Worcestershire, Panko crumbs & stale bread. I also added 1/4 cup of Italian dressing in lieu of olive oil. I did bake the meatballs rather than fry them. Ping Pong size, 30 minutes at 350. I finished cooking meatballs in slow cooker on high, in basic red pasta sauce for about another hr.

I took them to our Super Bowl party and they flew out of my crockpot! It was not only cool that my team won, but I came home with an empty crockpot. Wow! I felt like I won the Lombardi trophy!  Thank you.

text:
This recipe is AMAZING!!! I have been looking for a great meatball recipe and this is it! The base of this recipe is wonderful - it has a great taste and texture. I will change a couple things to fit my family's taste next time though: buy the = parts meatloaf mix meat, use 1 1/2 c. bread crumbs, 3/4 c. water max, 1/4 tsp. onion powder.  I substituted Italian seasoning in place of Italian parsley. I used 1/2 tsp. dried minced garlic because that is what I had on hand; it turned out fine but I will use fresh next time. I baked 1 1/2" meatballs in the oven at 400'f instead of frying them.  I put them in for 30 minutes uncovered, checking temp at 20 min.  I added a dash of hot sauce to the red sauce when heating the balls and sauce up together..

I halved this recipe since I'm cooking for two.  Next time I will make the full batch and freeze half.  These are not exact, but are close to the meatballs found in our local Italian places in North Central West Virginia.  I omitted the parsely because I didn't have any and used store bought grated Parmesan because that's what I had on hand.  I did not fry, I boiled them in water and then cooked them in sauce.  I use some of the water from the boil to add to my homeade sauce.  Definitely try this with all three meats - the results are worth it!

UPDATE: GAVE A BAG OF FROZEN MB TO MY PARENTS. THEY USUALLY LIKE EVERYTHING I SEND THEIR WAY, BUT EVEN MY DAD DISLKIED THESE (HE THOUGHT THEY WERE TURKEY MB'S!!!). These were allright. They certainly are not my mother's MB's, but decent nonetheless. My mom cannot remember her recipe (she add. a dash of this & that) nor can she find her handwritten copy, so I guess I am stuck! Mom hasn't made her MB's in ages - and prob. won't  since my dad is now on a restricted diet (her "all beef" MB's are anything but healthy lol!), which is a darn shame. I'd certainly post her version if I had it. :-) I pretty much followed this to the ltr. w/ the except. of a few ch. I add. a sm. (finely) minced onion, used 1/2 Parm / 1/2 Romano cheese & subbed Italian bread crumbs for fresh bread b/c I didn't have the latter. I end. up dbl. everything (my store only sold indiv. pkg. of ea. meat - in 1 lb. increments) & only using 3 c. worth of breadcrumbs (which was plenty, IMHO) that I soaked in ~ 2 c. lukewarm milk. This made a TON of meatballs (I had to use 3 cookie sheets!!!). Made subs (sub rolls were Garlic Bread Fantastique recipe, also on this site), add. meatballs/sauce (MB baked at 375 deg. for 25 min., then popped into spaghetti sauce & warmed on the stove) & topped w/ shredded mozza. Broiled for a few min. to brown the cheese & viola - restaurant-quality subs! I still think these MB's are pretty bland (comp. to mom's), but that's just me. Chips were an easy side. Tx. Geanine. :-)

text:
This is a great recipe.  I made more than the original recipe, using 1.5 lbs. ground chuck, .75 lbs. ground veal and .75 lbs. ground pork, 3 eggs, 3 garlic cloves, 3 T. parsley, 1.5 cups of freshly grated romano and 3 cups of a combination of fresh bread crumbs and Progresso Italian bread crumbs.  I only needed 1 1/2 cups of water/whole milk.  I baked the 2 inch meatballs on parchment paper in the oven for 45 minutes at 350 degrees, turning them after 25 minutes.  I then threw them into a saucepan with Marinara sauce for 15 minutes. The only issue I experienced was "oozing" cheeze while baking.  While it didn't affect the overal flavor, it made a little bit of a mess to clean up.    Overall a very tasty recipe.

text:
This was a great recipe and the first time I had ever made homemade meatballs. I used equal parts hamburger and spicy italian sausage ( our local grocery store sells an aweseom homemade version). I also added some onion to the mixture. The water really did make a difference, b/c 2 cups of breadcrumbs is a lot! I made some in a skillet on the stove top and baked the rest in the oven at 325 for about 45 minutes. They were so delicious and had a nice kick to them. For the ones I made in the skillet I added diced italian tomatoes and a small can of italian herbed tomato paste. We used them for meatball subs. Terrific. I froze the oven baked meatballs for future dinners. I will make these again!
